Carman £12 15s. 9d. ,, 29 REPORT OF THE COUNCIL of the METROPOLITAN BOROUGH OF WANDSWORTH For the Year ended 31st March, 1911. Election of Mayor. i. At the Meeting of the Council on the 9th November, 1910, Alderman Archibald Davis Dawnay, J.P., was unanimously re-elected Mayor of the Borough. Address to the Mayor. 2. The Council at its Meeting on the 19th October, 1910, resolved unanimously:— "That the best thanks of the Council be presented to Alderman Archieald Davis Dawnay, J.P., for his able, courteous, and impartial conduct in the Chair, and for the time and attention bestowed by him in the discharge of his duties as Mayor of this Borough." 3. The General Purposes Committee were instructed to prepare and settle an Address expressing; the Council's high appreciation of Alderman Dawnay's services. 4. The following Address was accordingly engrossed, framed, sealed with the Common Seal of the Council and presented to Alderman Dawnay at the Meeting of the Council on the 9th November:— 3o METROPOLITAN BOROUGH OF WANDSWORTH. Population. Area. Rateable Value. 332,843. 9,199 acres. ^2,129,429. To Archibald Davis Dawnay, Esq , J.P. We, the Aldermen and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough ot Wandsworth, desire to convey to you our thanks for the valuable services you have rendered to the Borough as Mayor and as a Justice of the Peace during your second year of office. 4 This period was notable owing to the lamented death of our late Sovereign King Edward VII., and it became your duty to proclaim at Wandsworth the accession of His present Majesty King George V. In the various functions and ceremonies arising out of these events you represented this Borough most worthily and with befitting dignity. You have extended your philanthropy, as in your previous year of office, to all parts and classes of the Borough, and we heartily thank you for this and for the hospitality which you have dispensed on so many occasions. Our thanks are also due to the Mayoress for the gracious manner in which she has so readily taken part in the discharge of the numerous social and public duties appertaining to the office. It is with great gratification that we learn that you have consented to be nominated for the third time in succes-ion. The coming year will be distinguished as the Coronation Year of Their Majesties King George V. and Queen Mary, when your experience of the office will be of the utmost value, and we sincerely wish you health and strength to carry out successfully the arduous duties which will devolve upon the Mayor of this large and populous Borough. Sealed by order, (Signed) J. W. Lorden, Ex-Mayor. Hen. Geo. Hills, Town Clerk. L.S 9th November, 1910. Presentation to the Mayor. 5. Alderman Lorden, L.C.C., on behalf of the subscribers, presented to the Mayor, as a mark of appreciation of his services in the discharge of the duties of Mayor during the past year, two Silver Dessert Dishes to match the Dessert Service presented last year. Presentation to the Mayoress. 6. Councillor Wise, on behalf of the subscribers, presented to Mrs. Dawnay a pearl and diamond brooch in velvet case with silver gilt shield engraved with the Borough Arms, and inscription inside, as a mark of 31 tion of her services in the discharge of the duties of Mayoress during the past year. Obituary. 7. The Council regrets to record the death, on the 4th December, 1910, of Councillor Roach, and on the 11th March, 1911, of Councillor Bates. Councillor Bates had been a Member of the Council since 1906 and Councillor Roach since 1909. Casual Vacancies. 8. The vacancies caused by the death of Councillors Roach and Bates were filled by the election of Mr. George Frederick Doland and Mr. John Thomas Hallinan respectively. In neither case was a Poll necessary, there being only one nomination received. Church Services. 9. The Mayor, Aldermen, Councillors, and principal officers of the Council, attended in State services at the following churches in the Borough, viz. :— loth April, 1910 Parish Church of Tooting, St. Nicholas, Church Lane. 10th July, 1910 St. Saviour's, Victoria Road, Clapham. 18th December, 1910 Parish Church of Wandsworth, All Saints, High Street. 15th January, 1911 Parish Church of Clapham, Holy Trinity, Clapham Common. 12th February, 1911 Parish Church of Putney, St. Mary, High Street. 12th March, 1911 Parish Church of Streatham, St. Leonard's, Streatham High Road. 10. The Council also attended, on the day of the funeral of the late King Edward VII., a Memorial Service at the Wandsworth Parish Church. Clapham Charities. 11. The period for which Councillor Bulcraig, J.P., Mr. A. Glegg, J.P., Mr. J. G. Kipling and Mr. E. C. Pannett were appointed to act in the administration of the Clapham Charities having expired the Council appointed Alderman A. U. Dawnay, J.P. (Mayor), Councillor Duncan, Councillor Yeowell, and Councillor Young its representatives to act in the administration of such Charities for a period of four years from the 24th October, 1910. 32 Putney Charities. 12. Mr. F. Newens, of 167, High Street, Putney, was reappointed to act in the administration of the Benjamin Hunt Bigg Charity, for the period of four years from the 15th October last. Thomas Martyn's Foundation. 13. In February, 1911, the Council considered the draft scheme of the Board of Education in the matter of Thomas Martyn's Foundation (otherwise the Watermen's School) at Putney. The draft scheme provided that the Governing Body of the Foundation was to consist of two representative Governors appointed by the London County Council, two by the Borough Council, and one by licensed watermen of Putney, and five cooptative Governors being residents of Putney. The first cooptative Governors, nine in number, were named in the scheme and were to be appointed for life. Representative Governors were to hold office for three years and co-optative Governors (except those named in the scheme) for 5 years. The present school was to be closed and the mistress pensioned at the rate of £50 per annum. A portion of the income was to be applied in clothing Junior Foundationers (not exceeding 30) resident in Putney, Wandsworth, Fulham, and Barnes, and being children of licensed watermen attending any public elementary school or other school approved by the Governors; and the residue of the income was to be applied in assisting Senior Foundationers to continue their education by means of apprenticeships or other modes of technical or industrial education. The gross yearly income of the Foundation is at present £411 14s. 8d. This Council approved of the proposed scheme, and the Board of Education were so informed. Streatham Charities. 14. Councillor Laceby was re-appointed and Councillor A. D. Robinson, M.A., L.L.B., appointed Representative Trustees of the Streatham Non-Ecclesiastical Charities for a period of four years from the 25th January, 1911, to fill the vacancies caused by the expiration of the period for which Councillor Laceby and Mr. T. Baines were appointed. 33 Weir Hospital Charity. 15. Alderman Hewett, Councillors Anderson, and Garrett, Junr., whose term of office expired on the 10th October last, were re-appointed the Council's representatives on the Committee of Management of the Weir Hospital Charity for the coming year. Tooting Charities. 16. Councillor the Rev. J. H. Anderson, M.A., was appointed the Council's representative to act in the administration of the Henry Smith Charity to fill the vacancy caused by the death of the late Mr. J. Perry. Wandsworth Charities. 17. 1 he period for which Councillor Buchanan and Mr. J. V. Elliott Taylor, J.P., were appointed Representative Trustees of the Wandsworth Consolidated Charities having- expired the Council re-appointed Councillor Buchanan and appointed Councillor Plumridge Representative Trustees for a period of four years from the 15th April, 1911. Metropolitan Water Board. 18. Alderman Lorden having been appointed a representative of the London County Council on the Metropolitan Water Board, resigned his position as the representative of this Council on such Board, and the Council on the 15th June last unanimously elected Alderman Hewett to fill the vacancy. W ands worth Technical Institute. 19. Councillor J. A. Robinson was, on the 5th April, 1911, appointed a Member of the Governing Body of the Wandsworth Technical Institute until the 31st July, 1912, to fill the vacancy caused by the resignation of Councillor Buchanan. Arms Shields. 20. The Mayor presented to the Council three shields of the Arms of the City of Cardiff. Death of King Edward VII. 21. The Members of the Council were deeply grieved by the death of his late Majesty King Edward VII., and at the Meeting of the Council on the nth May, 1910, the following Address to His Majesty King George V. was scaled, viz.:— 34 "TO THE KING'S MOST EXCELLENT MAJESTY. "We, the Mayor, Aldermen, and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, desire at this time of mourning for your Majesty's late revered Father, to express our heartfelt sympathy with you and the Royal family in the grievous loss Your Majesty and the whole of Your Empire have sustained by the sad death of out beloved Sovereign King Edward the Seventh. "We recall with deep gratitude the great qualities of statesmanship and patriotism which His late Majesty always displayed in so eminent and successful a degree, especially in his zeal for the cause of International Peace, and we humbly pray that Your Majesty, following so noble an example, and with the blessing of Almighty God, may long reign over a prosperous and happy people. "And we most dutifully beg to assure Your Majesty of the profound devotion and loyalty which our Borough will ever have to your Person and Throne. 22. On the same day the Council also sealed the following Address to Her Majesty Queen Alexandra, viz.:— "TO HER MOST GRACIOUS MAJESTY QUEEN ALEXANDRA. "We, the Major, Aldermen, and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, respectfully desire to express our heartfelt sorrow at the sad bereavement which Your Majesty has suffered by the untimely death of your august Husband His late Majesty King Edward the Seventh. "His Majesty had endeared himself to all his subjects by his kindness of heart and by his generous support (in which Your Majesty always so kindly co-operated) of Institutions and Movements having for their object the advancement of the interests and happiness of his people. "We earnestly pray that strength and fortitude may be vouchsafed by an all-loving Providence, to sustain and comfort Your Majesty and the Royal Family in this hour of affliction. "Sealed by Order. {Signed) "ARCHIBALD D. DAWNAY, "Mayor. L.S. (Signed) "HEN. GEO. HILLS, , "Town Clerk." " Sealed by Order. (Signed) "ARCHIBALD D. DAWNAY, "Mayor. L.S. (Signed) "HEN. GEO. "I am, Sir, "Your obedient Servant, (Signal) "WINSTON S. CHURCHILL. "The Town Clerk "Wandsworth, S.W." "Home Office, Whitehall, " 16th June, 1910. "Sir. (Signed) "ALEXANDRA." 36 Proclamation of King George V. 25. A Royal Proclamation with respect to the death of His late Majesty King Edward VII. and the accession of His Majesty King Georee V. was read by the Mayor in front of the Council House on Monday, the 9th May, at 9 a.m. The Town Clerk and many Aldermen and Councillors were present. Coronation of King George V. 26. A Royal Proclamation with respect to the Coronation of His Majesty King George V. was also read by the Mayor from the Council House at noon on Thursday, the 21 st July. Memorial to King Edward VII. 27. The Council considered the steps which were being taken by the Lord Mayor to provide a Memorial to the late King Edward VII. and did not think it desirable to take any action to obtain contributions to the Mansion House Fund, but that a separate Memorial should be provided for the Borough. The Mayor issued an appeal to residents in the Borough for contributions for that purpose, and a Public Meeting was held at the Wandsworth Town Hall on the 26th January, 1911, at which the following resolution was passed, viz.:— "That the proposed memorial should take the form of some visible and tangible monument (whether a statue, fountain, arch, or other structure), with appropriate inscription, the particular kind of monument to be determined by the Mayor and a Committee to be formed by him, when the amount of subscriptions is approximately ascertained, but such memorial to be of British manufacture, British material, and designed by British artists." 28. Other Meetings were held in the Borough, and a sum of over £600 has been subscribed. The Committee appointed at the Meeting held at the Wandsworth Town Hall decided that the Memorial should take the form of a Statue of the late King Edward and should be placed at Tooting Broadway. The Council approved of the position suggested, and the Committee having inspected several designs accepted the offer of Mr. L. F. Roselieb, of Grafton Square, Clapham, to provide and erect the Memorial at the Tooting Broadway. Endeavours will be made for the statue to be completed and fixed early in November next. 37 Death of Prince Francis of Teck. 29. At the Meeting of the Council on the 2nd November, 1910, the Mayor stated he had sent the following telegram to Her Majesty the Queen, viz.:— "TO HER GRACIOUS MAJESTY THE QUEEN, " Marlborough House. "On behalf of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, the Mayor respectfully and dutifully expresses sincerest sympathy with your Majesty in your sad bereavement." and that he had received the following telegram in reply thereto:— " MAYOR OF WANDSWORTH. "I am commanded by the Queen to convey Her Majesty's heartfelt thanks to you for the sincere sympathy you express with Her Majesty on behalf of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth. "WALLINGTON." 30. At the same Meeting the following resolution was passed, viz.:— That the following Address be signed by the Mayor and Town Clerk, on behalf of the Council, and presented to their Majesties the King and Queen, viz.: "TO THEIR MOST GRACIOUS MAJESTIES KING GEORGE V. AND QUEEN MARY. "The Mayor, Aldermen, and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth humbly beg leave to offer to your Majesties their dutiful sympathy and condolence upon the loss sustained by the lamentable death of His Serene Highness Prince Francis of Teck. "The high character of Prince Francis and the energy shown by him in connection with the work of the Middlesex Hospital and other philanthropic institutions and movements were greatly valued by your Majesties' subjects, who are sincerely grieved at his death. "With the greatest devotion and respect, we remain, "Your Majesties' dutiful subjects, "ARCHIBALD D. DAWNAY, Mayor. "HEN. GEO, HILLS, Town Clerk 3« 31. The following reply was received from the Home Secretary:— "Home Office, Whitehall, "8th November, 1910 "Sir, "I have had the honour to lay before the King and the Queen the loyal and dutiful Address of the Mayor, Aldermen, and Councillors of the Metropolitan Borough of Wandsworth, expressing condolence with Their Majesties on the death of His Serene Highness Prince Francis of Teck, and I have to inform you that Their Majesties were pleased to receive the same very graciously. "I am, Sir, "Your obedient Servant, (Signed) WINSTON S. CHURCHILL. The Town Clerk, Council House, Wandsworth, S.W." Post Office. 32. In June last the Council petitioned the PostmasterGeneral to provide a Post Office for Wandsworth suitable for the needs of the town and solely devoted to postal duties. In reply the PostmasterGeneral stated that the postal and telegraph arrangements at present afforded in the parish of Wandsworth were considered to be sufficient for the needs of the public, and that he regretted that he was unable to meet the Council's request for the establishment of a Post Office on premises devoted to post office work alone; and that it was found that the benefits accruing from such an arrangement would be altogether out of proportion to the considerable expenditure involved. The Council asked the Postmaster-General to reconsider the subject and called the attention of Sir Henry Kimber, M.P., to the matter. In reply to a question in the House of Commons by Sir Henry Kimber the PostmasterGeneral stated that the facilities at present afforded were considered sufficient and that there did not appear that there was any necessity for additional Sunday facilities. A similar reply was given to the Council's letter asking for the matter to be reconsidered. 39 Disorderly Houses. 33. Proceedings taken by the Council with respect to disorderly houses resulted in the following convictions being obtained, viz.:—For keeping a brothel and living on the earnings of an immoral woman, three months' imprisonment with hard labour; for keeping a brothel, three months' imprisonment with hard labour; for permitting a house to be used for habitual prostitution, fined £10 and £,2 2s. costs; and for allowing a boy, 10 years of age, to be upon the premises, fined £10, with the alternative of one month's imprisonment in each case, to run consecutively. Writing on Pavements. 34. The following Bye-Law was made by the Council on the 8th March last, viz.:— "No person shall deface the footway of any street by writing or other marks." PENALTY. "Any person who shall offend against the foregoing Byelaw shall be "liable for every such offence to a fine not exceeding Forty Shillings." Quinquennial valuation. 35. The following Parliamentary Bills were considered by the Council, viz.:— London County Council (General Powers). London County Council (Tramways and Improvements). Coroners' Law and Deaths Certification (Amendment). London Electric Supply. Municipal Representation. Milk and Dairies. Education (Administrative Provisions). Music and Dancing. Representation of the People. Shops (No. 2). Water Supplies Protection. Daylight Saving. Local Authorities (Advertising Municipal Elections. 41 London County Council (General Powers). 36. Part IV. of this Bill contained provisions for the regulation of lamps, structures, etc., in front of buildings and proposed to authorise the County Council to consent to or require the removal of any case, board, stall, awning, or other thing used for the display of articles or advertisement which extends beyond the exterior of any building and beyond the general line, or overhangs the public way. Part V. proposed to repeal the existing provisions with respect to the manufacture and sale of ice creams, and contained new provisions, and provided that proceedings might be taken by the County Council in case of default by the Sanitary Authorities. Clause 31 would have required the consent of the County Council to the construction of subways or passages under streets. Clause 32 extended the provisions of section 3 of the Metropolis Management (Amendment) Act, 1890, so as to enable Metropolitan Borough Councils to execute necessary works of repair to footways as well as to carriageways, and to recover the expense thereof from the adjoining owners. This clause was inserted upon the suggestion of this Council. Clause 33 proposed to amend section 205 of the Metropolis Management Act, 1855, so as to make employers liable for damage done by their servants to property belonging to Councils. This Council presented a petition against the provisions of Part IV., asked for the substitution of the Borough Councils for the County Council in clause 31, and approved of the provisions of clauses 32 and 33. Councillors Cundall and A. D. Robinson, M.A., LL.B., attended on behalf of this Council, a Conference of representatives of Metropolitan Borough Councils, at which the following resolutions were passed, viz.:— 1—That this Conference of representatives of the Metropolitan Borough Councils emphatically protests against the unnecessary encroachments upon the powers and duties of the Metropolitan Borough Councils contained in the London County Council (General Powers) Bill of the present session of Parliament. 2—That in the opinion of this Conference, Clause 19 (Regulations and control of certain lamps, structures, etc.), and Clause 20 (Council may require the removal of cases, boards, etc.) of the Bill are particularly objectionable in so far as they seek to confer powers on the London County Council at present exercisable by the Borough Councils with regard to certain projections on or over the public way, more especially as the matters referred to in Clause 19 are sufficiently provided for by Section 164 of the London Building Act, 1894, which empowers the London County Council to make Bye-laws in respect thereof, and vests the administration of such Bye-laws in the Borough Councils. 42 3.—That this Conference is strongly opposed to the proviso to Clause 25, Part V. of the Bill (Ice Cream), which provides, in case of default by the Sanitary Authority, that the County Council may take proceedings as in a case under the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, the Conference being of opinion that the granting of this power to the London County Council is unnecessary and derogatory to the Borough Councils. 4—That this Conference is of opinion that Clause 31 of the London County Council (General Powers) Bill, 1911, should be strenuously opposed by the Metropolitan Borough Councils unless the Borough Councils are made the sole Authorities to exercise the powers sought in the clause in question. 37. Part IV. of the Bill was opposed before the Committee of the House of Commons by this and other Borough Councils and others, and the Committee intimated that they were unanimously of opinion that that part of the Bill should not be proceeded with, and that the matters dealt with should not be under the sole control of the County Council. Part V. (which related to ice cream), which was also objected to by this Council, was withdrawn. The Town Clerk gave evidence in support of clause 32, and the clause was passed by the Committee. Clause 33 was opposed by omnibus companies, and was struck out. The Bill as amended was passed, and received the Royal assent on the 18th August. London County Council (Tramways and Improvements). 38. This Bill proposed to authorise the County Council to construct and work new tramways, to alter and reconstruct existing tramways, widen streets, and carry out other works. The Bill did not include any new tramways or reconstruction of tramways in this Borough. Clause 21 authorises the County Council to acquire and use for the purposes of its tramways the premises known as 31, Streatham Hill. The County Council agreed to the suggestion of this Council that a strip of land in front of the premises should be given up and added to the public way. Clause 27 extended for two years from the passing of the Bill the time limited for the compulsory purchase of land at High Street and York Road, Wandsworth. Clause 31 proposed to authorise the County Council to erect shelters or waiting rooms for tramway passengers, and with the consent of the road authority to use for that purpose portions of the streets. Clause 35 proposed to authorise the County Council to attach to any lamp-posts, poles, standards, or similar erections, on highways on or near to the route of any tramways signs indicating the position of stopping places. The Conference which considered the General Powers Bill 43 above referred to also considered this Bill, and were of opinion that clause 31 should be so amended as to enable the road authorities to attach conditions to their consent to the use of portions of streets for shelters, and to require the removal of such sheltersif deemed necessary, and that the provisions of clause 35 were objectionable, and should be amended so that the attachments in question shall not be made except with the consent and approval of the local authority; that such consent shall not constitute a perpetual easement; that the proposed signs shall be maintained by the County Council, and that complete protection should be given to the Borough Councils with regard to the maintenance and control of lamp-posts. This Council and four other Councils appeared before the Committee of the House of Commons in opposition to clause 35, when the London County Council intimated that the clause would be amended so as to provide that the County Council shall indemnify the owner of lamps against any damage occasioned by any attachment, and that nothing in the clause should be deemed to require the owner to retain any lamp when not required for his purpose. With those amendments the clause was allowed to proceed, and the Bill received the Royal assent on the 18th August. Coroners' Law and Deaths Certification (Amendment). 3g. The object of this Bill was to amend the law relating to Coroners and Death Certification so as to give effect to many of the recommendations of the Departmental Committee of 1908 and of the Death Certification Committee of 1893. This Council petitioned in favour of the Bill, which was, however, dropped. London Electric Supply. 40. The London Electric Supply Act, 1908, constituted the London County Council the purchasing authority (in lieu of the Borough Councils) in respect of the undertakings of nine of the fourteen companies authorised to supply electricity in London. Under the provisions of the present Bill the County Council will become the purchasing authority with respect to the undertakings of the remaining five companies, but they will not be able to purchase the undertaking of one company without purchasing the undertakings of all. The Council petitioned in favour of the Bill, which received the Royal assent on the 28th November, 1910. 44 Municipal Be presentation. 41. The Council presented a petition in favour of this Bill, which was to allow Municipal Authorities to adopt for their elections a system of proportional representation. The Bill was not proceeded with. Milk and Dairies. 42. The main objects of this Bill were to provide for the more effective registration of dairies and dairymen; the inspection of dairies and the examination of cows, the prohibition of milk from a dairy which would be likely to cause infectious disease; and the issue of regulations for securing the supply of pure and wholesome milk. This Council petitioned against the provisions of the Bill, which would have conferred on the Local Government Board extensive powers of making orders and regulations, and disposing of matters which are at present dealt with by magistrates, and the transfer of certain powers of Borough Councils to the County Council. The Council approved of clause 8 of the Bill, which provided that a warranty or invoice should not be available as a defence in proceedings under the Sale of Food and Drugs Act with respect to to milk. The Bill did not reach second reading. Education (Administrative Provisions). 43. This Bill proposed to remove from the Education Authority the final responsibility of deciding whether a child was or was not underfed, and to impose that duty upon the school doctor, the Medical Officer of Health, or other medical official. The Council petitioned against the Bill, which was not proceeded with. Music and Dancing. 44. This Bill was promoted by the London County Council, and its object was to effect an amendment of the law relating to licences for music and dancing in the administrative County of London as contained in the Disorderly Houses Acts, 1751 and 1818, and the Public Entertainments Act, 1875, in order to enable the London County Council (which is the authority to grant such licences in the County) to grant such licences at any time during the year, instead of being limited as at present to an annual licensing meeting now held in the month of November. This Council petitioned in favour of the Bill, which, however, was not proceeded with. 45 Representation of the People- 45. This Bill was again introduced by Sir Henry Kimber, Bart., M.P., its object being to make the representation of the people in the House of Commons more nearly proportioned to population. The Council petitioned in favour of the measure, but the Bill did not reach second reading. Shops 'No. 2). 46. This Bill was introduced by the Home Secretary, and proposed to amend and extend the Shops Regulation Acts, 1892 to 1904. The Council petitioned against the Bill, objecting particularly to provisions which would, in London, authorise the County Council to exercise the powers of Sanitary Authorities with reference to the ventilation and the provision of sanitary convenience in shops, being of opinion that matters should remain under the jurisdiction of the Borough Councils. The Bill was withdrawn. Water Supplies Protection. 47. The object of this Bill was to prohibit water undertakers sinking wells or constructing works unless such wells and works have been expressly approved by Parliament; to provide that where private supplies are injured by the abstraction of water for public supply the owner shall be entitled to compensation; and that any district from or through which water is conveyed shall be entitled to demand a share of such water for its own needs. The Council presented a petition in favour of the Bill. The Bill was considered by a Select Committee of the House of Lords, but did not reach the House of Commons. 48. No action was taken with reference to the other Bills above mentioned. Sir George Newnes, Bart. 49. The Council regrets to record the death, on the 8th June, 1910, of Sir George Newnes, But., who presented the Newnes Public Library to the Borough. A fund was raised by a Committee of residents with the view of providing a memorial and the Council, in March, 1911, accepted from such Committee a bust of Sir George, which has been placed in the corridor of the Newnes Library. 46 Bye Laws- Sanitary Conveniences. 50. Bye-laws with respect to the decent conduct of persons^ using the public lavatories and sanitary conveniences provided and maintained by the Council within the Borough have been made, and approved by the Local-' Government Board. Council's representative on the Metropolitan Paving Committee. Overhanging Lamps. &c. 54. Speed limit for motor traffic. 55. The Borough Council, upon further consideration, decided not to proceed with the proposal referred to in last year's report (page 53, par. 65), that a regulation should be made limiting the speed of motor traffic along High Street, Putney, to 10 miles an hour. The Council, however, recently re-considered the matter, and in reply to a communication from the London County Council decided to inform that Council that, in the opinion of the Borough Council, the circumstances of the case made it desirable that application should be made to the Local Government Board for the imposition of a reduced speed limit in High Street, Putney. Complaints 47 also received during the year of danger caused by the excessive speed at which motor vehicles travelled along Streatham High Road and Mitcham Lane. After full consideration the Council came to the conclusion that it was not desirable that any reduction should be made in the speed limit for motor traffic there, the subject of the complaints being a matter which, in the view of the Council, should be dealt with by the police. Boiler Skating in Streets. 56. In view of a fatal accident said to have been caused by roller skating in High Street, Clapham, the Borough Council repeated its application, made to the London County Council in April, 1910, for a Bye-Law to be made dealing with roller skating in streets. The County Council has not, however, yet made the proposed Bye-Law. Woodpaving Fund. 57. During the financial year ended 31st March last, woodpaving works were carried out in a number of main roads in the Borough. The cost of these works was £14,965, which, together with the sum of £3,337 for repayment of, and interest upon, loans in respect of works carried out in former years, was borne by the Woodpaving, &c (Short Loans Substitution) Fund. As reported last year the sum of £3,000 was allocated to the Fund from the ordinary estimates, but even with this assistance there was only the small balance of £650 to the credit of the Fund at the end of the year. In view of the extensive woodpaving works required to be executed in the near future in connection with the construction of tramways, and the expense of ordinary repairs and renewals, the Council decided to increase the rate levied for the purposes of the Fund from 1½d. to 2d. in the so as to place it on a more satisfactory footing. It was, however, found possible to make such a reduction in the ordinary estimates of the Highways Committee for 1911-12, that the increase in the rate for the Woodpaving Fund will not increase the total amount of the rate to be raised for the Committee's purposes for the current year. Mitcham Lane, Southeroft Road, and Wimbledon Road Tramways. 58. The construction of the London County Council tramways in Mitcham Lane and Southeroft Road and along Wimbledon Road referred to in last year'sreport (pages 56 and 57, pars. 76 and 77), has been completed. The lines, after inspection by the Board o£ 48 Trade, were opened for traffic in November last. The London County Council having found it impracticable to carry out the proposed improvement at the corner of Mitcham Lane and Babington Road in accordance with the deposited Parliamentary plan, a fresh line of widening at this point was agreed between the Borough Council and the County Council. Nearly. all the widenings required in connection with these tramways have been effected. Steps are being taken by the County Council with the view of executing the remaining improvement at an early date. Southfield Tramways. 59. The Borough Council has on several occasions during the past year had before it the subject of the suggested provision by the London County Council of a line of tramways between High Street, Wandsworth, and Southfield. During recent years extensive building operations have taken place in the district immediately westward of Merton Road, and a large residential population has sprung up there. On the eastern side of Merton Road, and at the southern end of that road adjoining the County boundary, there still remain tracts of land awaiting development. Means of communication between this district and other parts of London are at present limited, and a tramway connection with the County Council's existing system would be of great benefit to the residents. Two alternative routes have been suggested for the proposed tramways from High Street, Wandsworth. One would follow Merton Road throughout to the County boundary, and the other would leave Merton Road at the junction of Wimbledon Park Road and follow the latter road to Southfield railway station. The Borough Council has received deputations on two occasions in favour of the former route, and representations in support of that proposal were made to the Borough Council from a largely-attended public meeting of residents in the district affected. After careful consideration of all the circumstances, the Borough Council came to the conclusion that the route following the Merton Road to the County boundary was the most suitable for the proposed tramway. 60. The views of the Borough Council on the subject were communicated to the London County Council and a deputation, consisting of the Mayor (Alderman Dawnay, J.P.), Councillors 49 Garrett, Jackson and Wise, attended before a Sub-Committee of the County Council in support of the Borough Council's proposal. The matter is now under the consideration of the County Council. Clapham Park Road Tramways. 61. The London County Council had under consideration during the past year a proposal to construct a tramway from Clapham Cross to Brixton, via Clapham Park Road and Acre Lane, and suggested a conference with representatives of the Borough Council on the subject. After further consideration, however, the County Council dropped the proposal and the conference was not therefore necessary. Bedford Hill. 62. With the view of improving the part of Bedford Hill, Balham, adjoining Tooting Common, the Borough Council filled in the ditch and formed a footpath alongside the road, and provided the necessary gullies. The London County Council surrendered the strip of the Common required for the improvement, but declined to make any contribution towards the cost of the work. High Street, Clapham, widening. 63. The setting back of the projecting buildings between Nos. 82 and 98, High Street, Clapham, has been completed and the land added to the public way paved. The total cost of the widening was £3,627 5s. 4.d. The London County Council promised to contribute one-third of the cost, the contribution not to exceed the sum of £1,167. Merton Road Widening. 65. The widening of Merton Road, Southfield, in front of Burr Terrace and St. Barnabas Terrace, has now been completed. The total cost of the improvement was as follows, viz.:- Burr Terrace, £301 19s. 11d. St. Barnabas Terrace, £272 16s. 7d.; total, £574 16s. 6d. The Improvements Committee of the London County Council intimated that they were willing to recommend that Council to contribute two-thirds (not exceeding £182) of the cost of the 50 widening at St. Barnabas Terrace, subject to the Borough Council agreeing to contribute one-third of the nett cost of the widening by the County Council of Wimbledon Park Road, between St. Michael's Church and Standen Road. The Borough Council did not, however, see its way to agree to this condition, as the latter improvement was only necessary in the event of tramways being constructed there, and the Borough Council was of opinion that Merton Road was the more suitable route for such tramways. The County Council was not asked to contribute towards the cost of the widening at Burr Terrace. Mitcham Boad Widening. 66. Proposals made to the Borough Council with regard to the sale of the two pieces of surplus land in Mitcham Road, Tooting, acquired in connection with the widening of that road, were dealt with by the London County Council as that Council is contributing two-thirds of the cost of the improvement. The County Council was not, however, able to bring the negotiations to a successful conclusion, and the land is still in hand. Putney to Wandsworth Tramways. 67. Under the London County Council (Tramways and Improvements) Act, 1910, the County Council obtained powers to construct tramways along High Street, Putney, Putney Bridge Road, and High Street, Wandsworth, to connect the existing tramways at Putney with those in York Road, Wandsworth. The overhead system of traction will be adopted in High Street, Putney, and in Putney Bridge Road, the remainder of the route being worked on the underground conduit system. Owing to the extensive widenings which will be necessary in High Street, Wandsworth, the County Council decided to proceed first with the construction of the part of the line between Putney Bridge and the southern end of Putney Bridge Road. The approval of the Board of Trade was obtained to the proposals with regard to this section, and the works are now in hand. With the exception of the part of the road by the railway bridge near Point Pleasant, the tramway tracks will be paved with wood, the Borough Council agreeing to pave the remainder of the carriage-way with wood within two years of the completion of the works executed by the County Council. 51 Granite setts will be used for paving the whole width of the road by the above-mentioned railway bridge. Arrangements have been made for a double line of tramways to be laid, with the exception of a short length near Brewhouse Lane. The County Council was urged to construct this section also as a double line but, to the regret of the Borough Council the County Council found it impossible to adopt the suggestion. This is the only part of the tramway constructed as a single line. One-third of the total nett cost of the necessary widenings will be defrayed by the Borough Council, and the County Council will contribute two-thirds of the cost of the improvements recently carried out by the Borough Council in Putney Bridge Road. Roe Bridge Widening. 68. At the request of the Borough Council the London County Council, by arrangement with the Surrey County Council, has now carried out the widening- of Roe Bridge, carrying Mitcham Lane over the river Graveney at the County boundary. Streatham High Road. 69. The total cost of the paving and other works for which this Council was responsible, executed in Streatham High Road in connection with the construction of tramways there, was £14,251 gs. 10d., exclusive of certain work at Streatham Common which has not yet been carried out, owing to the County Council not having given the necessary consent. 70. The London County Council having declined to give permission to the Borough Council to round off the corner of Streatham Common at the junction of Streatham Common North and Streatham High Road, until the proposed improvement at the opposite corner of Streatham Common North has been effected, the Borough Council asked the County Council to carry out the latter widening in accordance with the agreement entered into between the County Council and the Borough Council in connection with the construction of tramways along Streatham High Road. The Borough Council was informed in reply that the Improvements Committee of the County Council were of opinion that it would not be advisable to take any steps at present to acquire the property needed for the improvement at the junction 52 of the northern side of Streatham Common North with the eastern side of Streatham High Road, as it appeared likely that an application would be made for the County Council's approval of plans for the development of the property, when the land needed could probably be secured free of cost. 71. The London County Council also adhered to its refusal to allow the Borough Council to form a proper footpath on the western side of Streatham High Road where it abuts upon Streatham Common. 72. These matters will continue to receive the attention of the Borough Council. 73. The matter is now being dealt with by the County Council. Summerstown Improvement. 74. The total cost of the improvement was £109 8s. 9d. Road Board Schemes. 75. (b) Tar-spraying main roads in the Borough. 53 The last mentioned proposal was not, however, entertained by the Road Board. The Council has also under consideration a proposal for the diversion of Upper Richmond Road, Putney, at the County boundary at Priests' Bridge, by the construction of a new road across private property, so as to abolish the sharp corners in the road there. The larger part of the improvement is in the County of Surrey, and the Council is in communication with other authorities affected with the view of the scheme being- submitted to the Road Board in the near future. 77. In connection with the woodpaving of Upper Richmond Road, between Roehampton Lane and Priory Lane, the Borough Council is endeavouring to make arrangements with the Barnes Urban District Council for narrow strips of Barnes Common to be added to the public way in order to make the path adjoining the Common of an uniform width. 78. The owner of Nos. 191 to 203, Upper Richmond Road, Putney, having given notice of his intention to convert those premises into shops, the Borough Council took the opportunity of effecting a widening of the road in front, in accordance with the plan approved some years ago. As the alterations to the buildings were about to be proceeded with, and satisfactory terms could not be arranged with the owner, it became necessary for the Council to put in force its powers for the compulsory acquisition of the strip of land. When the matter came before the jury the compensation estimated by the claimant's witnesses varied from £2,886 54 to £3,216, and the jury awarded £1,750. The Council's sealed offer was £500. The purchase having been completed, the land was thrown into the public way, and the necessary paving works executed at a cost of about £330. Warple Way and Fairfield Street Widening. 79. Overhead Telegraph Lines. 86. During recent years the Council has received many complaints from residents in the Borough of the erection by the Post Office Authorities of telegraph poles and wires in the streets. The Council endeavours to arrange for the laying of the wires underground in cases where their erection on poles would be likely to cause obstruction and annoyance, and has been successful in preventing poles being fixed where they would have been most undesirable. Recently the Council withheld its consent to the erection of poles in a number of streets, and suggested to the Post Office Authorities that underground lines would be more suitable in the localities affected. The PostmasterGeneral stated, however, that he felt bound, acting as he did in the interests of the public, to press for the Council's consent to overhead lines in the following roads, viz.:— (a) In Welham Road, Streatham, between Rectory Lane and Salterford Road ; (b) In Wimbledon Park Road, Southfield, from existing overhead line there to existing overhead line in Granville Road; (c) In Putney Bridge Road, Southfield, between Deodar Road and 137, Putney Bridge Road; (d) In Station Road and Fernlea Road, Balham; Emmanuel Road and Haverhill Road, Clapham South, from a point in Station Road near the junction of Culmore Road to a point in Haverhill Road near the junction of Midmoor Road; (g) In Burntwood Lane, Springfield, from a point near Garratt Lane to the junction of Tranmere Road. It was stated that if the required consent were not forthcoming a difference would be deemed to have arisen between the Postmaster-General and the Council which would have to be 57 determined by a Police Magistrate, and, on appeal, by the Railway Commissioners, and with the view of an amicable settlement being arrived at, a Conference was arranged between the Town Clerk, the Borough Engineer and the Solicitor, and the Solicitor and one of the Assistant Secretaries to the Post Office, to discuss the subject. The matter received careful consideration and ultimately the Council, in view of all the circumstances, decided not to object to the proposals of the Post Office, subject to the following conditions, viz.:— (a) That the proposed telegraph lines in Station Road, across Bedford Hill, Balham, and across Putney Bridge Road, Southfield, opposite Deodar Road, be placed underground. (b) That the poles in Welham Road, Streatham, Putney Bridge Road, Southfield, Fernlea Road, Balham, Emmanuel Road and Haverhill Road,. Clapham South, and Burntwood Lane, Springfield, be of creosoted wood, the lower part of the poles to be lagged with painted wooden laths, and the poles to be similar in every respect to the specimen pole erected opposite the Council House in 1908. (c) That the poles in Wimbledon Park Road, Southfield, be of iron. (d) That the poles in Emmanuel Road be placed in the kerb of the footpath on the side of the road nearest Tooting Common. (e) That, in the event of tramways being constructed on an overhead system of traction along Wimbledon Park Road, Putney Bridge Road, or Burntwood Lane, the telegraph wires in those roads shall, if the Postmaster-General has power and can obtain consent, be shifted to the tramway poles, and the telegraph poles removed. (f) That the poles, wires, and fire alarm posts be placed in such positions and the underground wires laid at such depths as may be agreed between the Borough Engineer and the representative of the Postmaster-General on the ground, and that the whole of the works be carried out to the satisfaction of the Borough Engineer. (g) That no part of any wire over any road or footway shall at any time be at a less height than twenty-five feet above such road or footway. (h) That not more than twenty-four wires be placed on any one pole, and that in the event of wires in excess of that number being required, the Postmaster-General shall, subject to the consent of the Council, construct an underground line along that portion of the route on which such greater number is required, in lieu of the corresponding portion of the overhead route, and shall, without prejudice to the question whether such poles and wires, or any of them, should be retained or re-erected for telephone distribution purposes, remove all such poles and wires. 58 (i) That where the telegraph poles, fire-alarm posts, and underground, wires are placed in parish roads under the care of the Council, the work of permanently reinstating the public way repairable by the Council be executed by the Council, and the cost thereof repaid by the Post Office authorities, in accordance with the scale of prices agreed to in the letters from the Postmaster-General, dated 9th May, 1903, and 4th April, 1908. In connection with this matter, it may be mentioned that in several recent cases in other Boroughs where the local authority objected altogether to the erection of overhead telegraph lines, the Postmaster-General, on appeal, obtained the necessary permission to place the wires overhead in the streets referred to in his application, his offer to compromise the matter by laying some of the wires underground having been refused. In some cases an order was made for the wires to be placed underground if the local authority would pay the additional expense. Southfield Slop Shoot. 87. Arrangements have been made with the owner of adjoining land for the straightening of the irregular boundary at the southern end of the Council's Southfield slop shoot. The exchange of lands was effected by an order of the Board of Agriculture. The old boundary followed the old course of the river Wandle, and this has been filled in and a fence erected on the new boundary. Sulina Road Depot. 88. The Council having discontinued the use of the small depot in Sulina Road, Streatham, held under agreement expiring Lady Day, 1912, arrangements were made for the Council to be released from the agreement, and possession of the depot was given up in March last. Conference on Educational Matters. 89. The annual Conference on educational matters between Members of the London County Council and Managers of Public Elementary Schools in the Battersea, Clapham, and Wandsworth Electoral Divisions, to which the Members of this Council's Education Committee were also invited, was held in November. A number of Resolutions were passed and forwarded to the London County Council, among them being one on the subject of the cost of education, in which it was suggested that the greater proportion ot the cost of national education should be met by increased Government grants. 59 New Schools. 90. Notice has been received from the London County Council of its intention to erect a new school for about 1,000 children, on part of the Furzedown site West Streatham, and to apply for statutory powers of purchase over a site for a school in Derinton Road, Tooting. London County Council Education Committee. 91. In view of the very large area and population of the Division, this Council passed a resolution requesting, the London County Council to appoint on its Education Committee a Member resident in the County Council Electoral Division of Wandsworth, and therefore acquainted with the educational needs of that Division. The County Council stated in reply that in appointing its Committees it was the practice to consult the wishes of Members, and that, with regard to the co-opted Members of the Committee, in the absence of any other qualification than residence in a particular locality, a person would not be eligible for co-option, and that the Council's letter would receive further consideration at the next re-appointment of Committees. A copy of the correspondence with the County Council was forwarded to the Chairman of each body of Managers in the Division, and a number of Managers expressed their concurrence in the resolution, and communicated their views to the County Council. Powers and Duties of Managers. 92. The Council has again urged the desirability of increasing the powers and duties of Managers, but was informed that the appropriate Committee of the County Council who considered this Council's communication did not see their way to recommend the County Council to take any action in the matter. School Managers. 93. The triennial appointment of this Council's representatives on the Bodies of Managers of Provided and Non-provided Schools in the Borough took place in November, 1910, the appointments being for the three years ending December, 1913. The question of applying to the appointments conditions as to the attendances of Managers and visits to Schools was considered, but the Council did not think it expedient to adopt such conditions. 6o Apprenticeships. 94. The Education Committee considered, on the motion of Councillor Renshaw, the subject of Apprenticeships, and submitted the following report thereon, which was adopted by the Council, viz.:— (a) We are of opinion that a constructive scheme should be carefully elaborated by the Education Authority that will enable deserving boys and girls to learn under proper conditions, directly they leave school a trade or suitable occupation which the parents should select where possible. (b) To do this we are of opinion that for apprentices the school age should be raised to the age considered necessary in each trade to learn that particular trade and to complete the apprenticeship. (c) That either premium agreements or trade apprenticeships in masters' and manufacturers' workshops and jobs should be instituted, so that the boy or girl can learn the trade or occupation chosen in working conditions and under the supervision of the employers' own foremen. (d) That hours of labour suitable to the trade chosen can readily be arranged 1with employers, it being an essential condition that time shall be allowed where desired for afternoon classes on one or two days a week, so that theory can be taught hand in hand with practice. (e) We suggest that boys or girls who gain Scholarship rewards should first have the option of choosing a scholastic or a trade training; where a trade is chosen an apprenticeship with an approved employer could be entered into for an agreed term of years. (f) We suggest for the consideration of the Education Authority that the Scholarship rewards to such children should be an apprenticeship or premium fund tor payment to the employers of a suitable premium according to the trade chosen, such premium being returned in the form of weekly wages. (g) We suggest that children other than those who gain Scholarships should have the same privileges as far as vacancies and trades can be found, but in their case the premium, if any, should be advanced by the Education Authority, and refunded in whole or in part by the parents by agreed instalments. (h) That apprentices should work the hours customary in the chosen trade, but in every case they should cease work sufficiently early to attend evening classes in technical subjects. (i) That the continued employment of the apprentices should be subject to good behaviour and satisfactory progress; in cases of bad conduct or unsuitability the agreement could be mutually cancelled and a due proportion of the premium money, if any, be refunded. (j) To induce parents to apprentice their boys we are of opinion that the premiums should be kept as low as possible, and suggest that £10 should be regarded in most trades as a sufficient premium, and that even this sum should be waived wherever the employer will agree to do so. (k) We suggest that all such apprentices should be subject to inspection by the Education Authority's representative from time to time in working hours and that such Inspector shall satisty himself that the conditions of employment and training are being reasonably fulfilled 011 both sides ; the employer should report twice yearly as to the conduct, punctuality, and progress of each apprentice. (l) That such wages as should be agreed upon, and suitable to the trade chosen, should be paid weekly to the apprentices, graduated and increased each year as experience is gained; such weekly wages to be set out in a schedule as part of the apprenticeship agreement. (m) That for the purposes of this scheme the number of boys allowed to each shop or job by Trade Union rules be increased as may be mutually agreed. 61 95. Copies were forwarded to the Lord Mayor of London, the City Corporation, the London County Council, the Metropolitan Borough Councils, and the representatives of the Borough upon the County Council, with a request that they would support the views of the Council. Four of the Borough Councils expressed agreement with the views of the report, and a number were in favour of the principle of the scheme. The suggestions of the Council were also favourably received by the Master Decorators' Association and the London Institute of Builders, who adopted reports on the lines of the Council's scheme. A Committee of the County Council considered the resolutions, and stated in reply, that whilst fully sympathising with the object in view, the Committee regretted they were unable to make any recommendations to the County Council in the matter, as the Council had no legal power to pay apprenticeship premiums as suggested. Central Schools. 96. The Council approved generally of a scheme proposed by the London County Council for the establishment as part of the elementary school system of London of a series of Higher Schools, to be termed " Central Schools," which would give their pupils a definite bias towards some kind of industrial or commercial work, and would take the place of the existing higher elementary and higher grade schools. The curriculum of each school is to be determined with a view to meeting the needs of the district, the pupils between 11 and 12 years of age, being selected from surrounding schools. It is proposed to have a separate body of Managers for each Central School, consisting of eight persons appointed by the Borough Council and four by the County Council. Wandsworth Baths. 97. The competition for the swimming trophy presented by Sir William Lancaster, J.P., and competed for annually by men resident in the Borough, was held on the 14th October, and was won by Mr. J Symons. Sir William Lancaster again gave a prize for the winner, as a memento of the occasion, and the Mayor (Alderman Dawnay) kindly provided a prize for the competitor who finished second. Women's Medal. 100. The competition for the medal for women residing in the Borough, presented by the late Mr. John Bell, J.P., was held on the 7th October, at the annual entertainment of the Wandsworth Swimming Club (Ladies' Section), and was again won by Miss N. Treversh. 63 Swimming Competitions for School Children. 101. Swimming competitions for school children were held at the Wandsworth Baths on the 14th October, and a free pass to the second-class bath, available during the following year, was awarded to the successful boy or girl from each school. The competitions are open to boys and girls from schools in the Borough attending the baths for instruction in swimming, the passes are available out of school hours and before seven o'clock in the evening. A large number of children and their parents were present, and the Mayor presided. There are 63 elementary schools in the Borough, 30 departments send pupils to the baths for instruction in swimming, and all entered for the competitions. The number of children taking part in the competitions was 138—68 boys and 70 girls. Storage of Cycles. 102. Several complaints having been received of cycles being stolen from the cycle room at the Wandsworth Baths, the Council decided to undertake the custody of cycles brought there by bathers, and to make a charge of one penny therefor. The receipts and the increased number of bathers who cycle to the baths show that the arrangement is fully appreciated by persons visiting the baths. Wandsworth Baths. 103. An improvement has been carried out at the Wandsworth Baths by covering in a small passage between the entrances to the first and second class swimming baths, which has proved a great convenience, especially when galas are held. A doorway has also been made between the first and second class baths, so that the second class bath can now be used for dressing purposes on these occasions. Swimming Baths. 104. An additional exit has been provided at the southern end of the gallery in the first class swimming bath; a doorway has been made and an iron staircase provided, which communicates direct with the embankment at the side of the building. Provision of Baths. 105. The Council being of opinion that additional swimming accommodation in covered buildings is required for the eastern side of the Borough, the question of providing such accommodation has been referred to a Committee, and is now under consideration. 64 Interments. 106. A new greenhouse has been erected at Wandsworth Cemetery at a cost of £139. Huguenot Burial Ground. 110. The Council has repaired a number of the tombstones and vaults in the Huguenot Burial Ground, East Hill, and has planted some fresh trees there. A local Committee have raised subscriptions for the purpose of providing a Memorial to the Huguenots. The memorial is of Portland stone, and will be erected on the north side of the ground facing East Hill. An inscription will be cut in the stone, and a list of Huguenot families interred in the burial ground carved on the plinth. Laying Out Land for Burials Wandsworth Cemetery. 111. It has been found necessary to lay out additional land for burials at Wandsworth Cemetery, including a piece of the ground at present let for recreative purposes. New roads are being formed and the necessary drainage works executed. Stealing Flowers from Graves. 112. As the result of complaints of flowers being stolen from graves a watch was kept, and a man caught taking flowers from a grave at Wandsworth Cemetery. He was charged with the offence, and on being brought before the Magistrate at the South-Western Police Court was sentenced to six weeks' hard labour. Cemeteries Committee. 113. The title of the Burials Committee has been altered to the "Cemeteries Committee." 66 APPORTIONMENTS. 114. General Report on Testings of Gas supplied to the Wandsworth Borough Council (1) by the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company; (2) by the Mitcham and Wimbledon Gas Company for the year ended 31st March, 1911. Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company. I have made the usual bi-weekly tests of this gas during the year ended 31st March, 1911, as regards Illuminating Power, Sulphuretted Hydrogen, Sulphur (other than sulphuretted hydrogen) and Pressure. In Table I. will be seen a summary of the monthly averages of these tests, while in Table III. are shewn curves representing the fluctuations of the Illuminating Power and of the Sulphur based on the weekly averages of these tests. By reference to Table I. it will be noted that the average illuminating Illuminating Power for the year ended 31st March, 1911, is 14.6 candles, a somewhat lower average than has hitherto obtained. In January, 1911, the maximum monthly average of 15.0 candles was reached, while April, May, June and September, 1910, and February and March, 1911, shew the minimum monthly average of 14.5. Hence while the average is somewhat lower as a whole, there has been considerable uniformity in the Illuminating Power. By reference to Table III., shewing the curve based 011 the weekly averages of the Illuminating Power, it will be seen that these have varied between a minimum of 14.1 (November, 1910) and a maximum of 15.5 (January, 1911). 136 The average number of grains of Sulphur (other than sulphuretted hydrogen) in 100 cubic feet of gas was for the whole year ended 31st March, 1911, 277. This is a satisfactory average being rather less than that of 1909 (29.5 grains) although slightly higher than that of 1910 (24.0 grains). The monthly averages (Table I.) vary between a minimum of 24.0 (September, 1910) and 30.6 grains (February, 1911) while the weekly averages (see Sulphur curve, Table III.) shew a minimum of 207 (March, 1911) and a maximum of 34.8 grains (February, 1911). Sulphur. Pressure. The pressure has not been excessive at any time during the year ended 31st March, 1911. In Table I. it will be observed that with an average for the whole year of 2.8 inches, the minima and maxima monthly averages were 2.7 and 3.1 respectively. Sulphuretted Hydrogen. At no time have I found this impurity in the gas during the Past year. Proposed New Burner and Calorific Tests. In my last Annual Report, for the year ended 31st March, 1910, I called attention to the Gas Companies (Standard Burner) Bill, in which the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company and the Brentford Gas Company proposed to join, having presented a report on the same to the Council, dated 31st December, 1909. In that report I stated that there seemed to be no valid objection to the adoption of the proposed new Standard Burner (the Metropolitan Argand Burner No. 2) by the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company. At the same time I strongly urged the institution of Calorific Power Tests, for information, with a view to the ultimate adoption of a Calorific Power Standard. Eventually, however, the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company withdrew from the Bill in March, 1910, and, to my regret, the matter dropped. Since that date the Brentford Gas Company having adopted a new Burner, very similar to but not identical with the Metropolitan Argand No. 2, successfully upheld in the High Court, in proceedings taken by the Chiswick Urban District Council, their right to use the same for the testing of their gas. 37 In January of this year (1911) the Engineer of the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company intimated to me that his Company considered they also had a right to use the new Brentford Burner for testing their Gas, and requested me to put the matter before the Wandsworth Borough Council. This I accordingly did and after consideration by the Council I finally reported on the whole matter at length on February nth, 1911, and made the following suggestions:— (1) That inasmuch as the new Brentford Burner so closely resembled the new Standard Burner (Metropolitan Argand No. 2) now in general use by the Metropolitan and other gas companies, and further since the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Company had previously expressed a desire to adopt this latter Burner (having assisted originally in promoting the Standard Burner Bill above alluded to) I suggested that for the sake of uniformity they should adopt this Standard Burner instead of the new Brentford Burner. (2) That inasmuch as a change was proposed to be made in connection with the testing of the Illuminating Power of the gas, the occasion seemed a favourable one for instituting at the same time tests for the Calorific Power of the Gas. The Company agreed to use the Metropolitan Argand Burne No. 2 for testing the Gas and to provide the necessary apparatus for testing the Calorific Power. Mitcham and Wimbledon Gas Company. I have made the usual tests of Illuminating Power, Sulphuretted Hydrogen and Pressure of this Gas at the testing place in Haydon's Road, South Wimbledon, and my results are shewn in Table II. annexed to this report. It will be seen that the average Illuminating Power for the Illuminating whole year ended 31st March, 1911, is 15.8 candles power. with a minimum of 15.2 candles (December, 1910) and a maximum of 16.8 candles (November, 1910) the statutory Illuminating Power being 15 candles. 138 Pressure. The pressure which is usually rather higher than that of the Wandsworth and Putney Gas Co., has shewn an average of 3.6 inches with a minimum of 2.6 and a maximum of 4.3 inches. Sulphuretted Hydrogen. This impurity has been absent from the gas at all testings made during the year ended 31st March, 1911. H. Wilson Hake, Ph.D., Gas Examiner. TABLE 1. REPORT OF THE WANDSWORTH DISTRESS COMMITTEE. From the 1st July, 1910, to 30th June, 1911. The Distress Committee was appointed by the Borough Council on the nth October, 1905, in accordance with the Unemployed Workmen Act (1905), and constituted as follows:— Appointment. Members of the Borough Council 12 Members of the Board of Guardians 8 Persons experienced in the relief of distress 5 Members of the Council:—Aldermen Cresswell, Hewett, Lorden, Penfold, and Robinson; Councillors Anderson, Couzens, Denny, Everett, Jackson, Plumridge and Prince. Members of Committee. Members of the Board of Guardians:—Rev. J. Cooney, Mr. G. J. Fowle, Mr. W. P. Melhuish, Mr. E. A. Miller, m.b., Mr. Percival Rees (Chairman), Lieut. E. A. Sanders, r.n., and Mr. A. Sullivan (one vacancy). Members experienced in the relief of distress, appointed for one year:—Rev. D. Tudor Craig, Mr. F. Nash, and Miss M. H. Pollock (two vacancies). A Sub-Committee of twelve members was formed, constituted as follows:—Mr. Percival Rees (Chairman); Alderman Cresswell, Councillors Couzens, Denny, and Jackson, Lieut. Sanders, r.n., Rev. J. Cooney, Mr. G. J. Fowle, Miss M. H. Pollock (three vacancies), and the Chairman and Members of the Central Body ex officio: the duties being to enquire and report as to condition of labour, to consider and classify the Record Papers when completed. Sub-Committee and reference. 180 Applications from unemployed persons were received at the office of the Distress Committee, 3, Church Row, The Plain, Wandsworth, during the winter months, from Men on Monday, Tuesday, Thursday and Friday, and from Women on Wednesday, between the hours of 9 a.m. and 12 o'clock noon. Reception at Office. The particulars entered on the Record Papers were investigated and verified by personal visits to the homes of the applicants, by the investigators, and references as to character were obtained from previous employers. No personal investigations were made outside the Borough. Investigation. The Sub-Committee considered the completed Record Papers and classified the applications into four divisions:— Preference, Eligible, Ineligible, and Disqualified. In recommending applicants to the Central Body as suitable for employment, migration, or emigration, the Sub-Committee gave preference to men of good character, and distinguished as far as possible, between the habitual "out of work" and the applicant who was unemployed through trade depression, or kindred causes. Classification. The wages of the men from this Borough employed on the Non Colony Works were paid on Saturday morning at the Office of the Committee; the week's work being from Monday morning to Friday night. The Rate of wages was 6d. per hour, except in the case of men working in Royal Parks, the wages there being 3s. 10d. per day, and full fares paid. Payment of Wages. The men sent to the Working Colonies receive 6d. per week,. in addition to their board and lodging, a weekly allowance being made to the family on the following scale:—10s. to the wife, 2s. for the first child under 14, 1s. 6d. for the second child under 14, and 1s. for each other child under 14 years; but in no case was 17s. 6d. to be exceeded. The allowances are paid at the homes of the men on Wednesdays. The men are allowed a furlough at the end of each month, their fares being paid for them. Family allowance. 181 Representatives of Wandsworth on the Centrai (Unemployed) Body for London. Rev. J. H. Anderson, M.A., Chairman of the Central Body and Chairman of Works Committee. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Central Body, 100.00 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Works Committee, 100.00 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Sub-Committee, 50.00 per cent. As ex officio member, attended meetings on other Standing Committees on 35 occasions. Mr. Percival Rees, Chairman of Finance Committee. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Central Body, 87.5 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Finance Committee, 100.00 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Works Committee, 33.3 per cent. Percentage of attendances at meetings of Finance Sub-Committee of Accounts, 100.00 per cent. 182 ATTENDANCES OF COMMITTEE. The work has been carried out by the Sub-Committee, no meeting of the full Committee having been called. ATTENDANCE OF SUB-COMMITTEE. Actual. Possible. Anderson, Councillor Rev. J.
